href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/private-firearm-sale-in-florida/" title="What is the Law for a Private Firearm Sale In Florida?">What is the Law for a Private Firearm Sale In Florida?</a></h3> <p class="meta dotted"><span class="dashicons-before user"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/author/matt-adika/" title="Posts by Matt Adika" rel="author">Matt Adika</a></span> <span class="dashicons-before folderb"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/category/firearms-blog/" rel="category tag">Firearms Blog</a></span> <span class="dashicons-before clock"><span>November 10, 2014</span></span></p> <div class="entry-content"> <img width="150" height="62" src="http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/private-gun-sale-florida.jpg?fit=150%2C62" class="attachment-blog-thumbnail size-blog-thumbnail wp-post-image" alt="private-gun-sale-florida" srcset="http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/private-gun-sale-florida.jpg?w=600 600w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/private-gun-sale-florida.jpg?resize=200%2C83 200w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/private-gun-sale-florida.jpg?resize=500%2C208 500w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/private-gun-sale-florida.jpg?resize=100%2C41 100w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/private-gun-sale-florida.jpg?resize=150%2C62 150w" sizes="(max-width: 150px) 100vw, 150px"> <h1>Private Firearm Sale In Florida</h1> <div class="entry"> <p>Florida has no law generally requiring a background check for a <strong>Private Firearm Sale In Florida</strong> or on the purchaser of a firearm when the seller is not a licensed dealer. However, the Florida Constitution permits counties to adopt laws that would require such background checks for sales occurring in or on “property to which the public has the right of access” within the county. The Florida Constitution states that, “[e]ach county shall have the authority to require a criminal history records check…in connection with the sale of any firearm occurring within such county.”<sup>1</sup> The term “sale” under this section “means the transfer of money or other valuable consideration for any firearm when any part of the transaction is conducted on property to which the public has the right of access.”<sup>2</sup> Concealed weapons permit holders are not subject to these laws.<sup>3</sup></p> <ol class="footnotes"> <li id="footnote_0_585" class="footnote">Fla. Const. art. VIII, § 5(b).</li> <li id="footnote_1_585" class="footnote"><em>Id.</em></li> <li id="footnote_2_585" class="footnote"><em>Id.</em></li> </ol> <p><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-25421" src="http://i0.wp.com/smartgunlaws.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/background-header.jpg?resize=500%2C41" alt="background-header" data-recalc-dims="1"><br> <img id="SA Basics" src="http://i2.wp.com/smartgunlaws.org/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/Factsheet-Orange1.jpg?w=500" alt="" name="Factsheet" align="right" border="0" data-recalc-dims="1"></p> <p>The most dangerous gap in federal firearms laws today is the “private sale” loophole.&nbsp; Although federal law requires licensed firearms dealers to perform background checks on prospective purchasers and maintain records of all gun sales, it does not require unlicensed “private” sellers to do so. An estimated 40% of all firearms sold in the U.S. are transferred by unlicensed sellers.<sup>1</sup></p> <p>According the U.S. Department of Justice, because federal law does not require universal background checks, <strong>“individuals prohibited by law from possessing guns can easily obtain them from private sellers and do so without any federal records of the transactions.”</strong><sup>2</sup> &nbsp;“The private-party gun market,” one study observed, “has long been recognized as a leading source of guns used in crimes.”<sup>3</sup>&nbsp; Although the private sale loophole is frequently referred to as the “gun show” loophole (because of the particular problems associated with gun shows), it applies to all private firearm sales, regardless of where they occur.<sup>4</sup></p> <p><img class="alignright size-full wp-image-25718" src="http://i2.wp.com/smartgunlaws.org/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/privatesales_animation_FINAL.gif?resize=250%2C500" alt="private gun sales and trafficking" data-recalc-dims="1">The growth of the Internet has significantly increased the ability of individuals prohibited from possessing firearms to find sellers willing to transfer firearms to them without background checks.</p> <ul> <li>As of September 2013, about 67,000 firearms were &nbsp;listed for sale online from private, unlicensed sellers.<sup>5</sup></li> <li>29% of ads by private sellers on Armslist.com (a popular website for firearm sales) were posted by high-volume private sellers&nbsp;who posted five or more ads over an eight-week period.<sup>6</sup></li> <li>According to an undercover investigation conducted by the City of New York, 62% of private online firearm sellers agreed to sell a firearm to a buyer even after the buyer had told the seller that he or she probably could not pass a background check.<sup>7</sup></li> </ul> <p>When private sellers don’t run background checks, people known to be dangerous can easily obtain guns, often with deadly consequences. For example, in 2012, a gunman killed three people, including his wife, and injured four others at a spa in Wisconsin, after buying a gun through a private seller he found online.&nbsp; The shooter was prohibited from purchasing guns due to a restraining order his wife had acquired against him, but was able to buy the gun anyway because the seller was not required to run a background check.<sup>8</sup></p> <p>In a 2007 report, the International Association of Chiefs of Police (IACP) stated that, because individuals who fail a background check can easily access firearms through private sales, “guns are far too easily acquired by prohibited possessors, and too often end up being used in gun crime and gun violence.”<sup>9</sup>&nbsp; The IACP concluded that “Congress, as well as state, local and tribal governments, should enact laws requiring that all gun sales and transfers proceed through” a federally licensed dealer.<sup>10</sup></p> <p><strong>Private sales represent a significant conduit for illegal gun trafficking.&nbsp;</strong></p> <ul> <li>The Bureau of Alcohol, Tobacco, Firearms &amp; Explosives (ATF) found that during one 29-month period, unlicensed sellers were involved in about one-fifth of illegal trafficking investigations nationwide and associated with nearly 23,000 trafficked guns.<sup>11</sup></li> <li>A study which used crime gun trace data from 53 U.S. cities for the years 2000–2002 found that laws regulating private handgun sales&nbsp;are strongly associated with fewer trafficked guns.<sup>12</sup></li> <li>A 2009 GAO report found that “secondary firearms — firearms resold following the first retail purchase from an FFL, or ‘used guns’ — are commonly trafficked to Mexico.”<sup>13</sup></li> <li>Another report observed that the lack of background check and record retention requirements for private gun transfers “continue to make it much easier for prohibited persons to purchase firearms and much harder&nbsp;for U.S. authorities to successfully trace how a firearm illegally reached Mexico.”<sup>14</sup></li> </ul> <p><img class="alignleft size-full wp-image-25717" src="http://i1.wp.com/smartgunlaws.org/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/privatesales-1-FINAL.jpg?resize=300%2C450" alt="privatesales-1-FINAL" data-recalc-dims="1"><strong>Gun offenders overwhelmingly obtain their guns through private sales.</strong> A survey of state prison inmates in 13 states who were convicted of gun offenses found that only 13.4% obtained the gun from a gun store or pawnshop, where background checks are required.<sup>15</sup> Nearly all (96.1%) of those inmates who were already prohibited from possessing a gun at the time of the crime obtained the firearm through an unlicensed private seller.<sup>16</sup></p> <p><strong>When background checks are required, they are extremely effective at keeping guns out of the hands of prohibited persons.</strong> Since the federal background check requirement was adopted in 1994, over two million prohibited persons have been denied a firearm transfer or permit.<sup>17</sup> &nbsp;In 2010 alone, more than 117,000 gun transfers were denied using the federal background check system.<sup>18</sup></p> <p><strong>Repeated polls have shown that over 90% of the American public supports laws requiring background checks on all gun purchasers,</strong> regardless of whether they buy weapons from licensed dealers or private sellers.<sup>19</sup> A survey conducted for the New England Journal of Medicine in January 2013 found that 84% of gun owners and 74% of NRA members also support requiring a universal background check system for all gun sales.<sup>20</sup></p> <p>As described below, the strongest laws require a background check at the point of sale for every gun transfer.&nbsp; Some additional states only require a background check when a gun is sold at a gun show, or require gun purchasers to obtain a license before purchasing a gun and issue the license only after a background check.&nbsp; For additional information in support of these laws,&nbsp;see our summaries on&nbsp;Gun Shows and Licensing Gun Owners &amp; Purchasers.</p> <p><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-25423" src="http://i2.wp.com/smartgunlaws.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/federal-header.jpg?resize=500%2C41" alt="federal-header" data-recalc-dims="1"></p> <p>Federal law imposes various duties on federally licensed firearms dealers.&nbsp; Firearms dealers must, among other things: (1) perform background checks on prospective firearm purchasers; (2) maintain records of all gun sales; (3) make those records available to law enforcement for inspection; (4) report certain multiple sales; and (5) report the theft or loss of a firearm from the licensee’s inventory.<sup>21</sup>&nbsp; Federal law imposes none of these requirements on <i>unlicensed</i> sellers, however.</p> <p>The Gun Control Act of 1968 provides that persons “engaged in the business” of dealing in firearms must be licensed.<sup>22</sup>&nbsp; Although Congress did not originally define the term “engaged in the business,” it did so in 1986 as part of the McClure-Volkmer Act (also known as the “Firearms Owners’ Protection Act”).&nbsp; That Act defined the term “engaged in the business,” as applied to a firearms dealer, as “a person who devotes time, attention, and labor to dealing in firearms as a regular course of trade or business with the principal objective of livelihood and profit through the repetitive purchase and resale of firearms.”<sup>23</sup></p> <p>Significantly, however, the term was defined to <i>exclude</i> a person who “makes occasional sales, exchanges, or purchases of firearms for the enhancement of a personal collection or for a hobby, or who sells all or part of his personal collection of firearms.”<sup>24</sup> According to a 1999 report issued by the Bureau of Alcohol, Tobacco, Firearms and Explosives (ATF), the current definition of “engaged in the business” often frustrates the prosecution of “unlicensed dealers masquerading as collectors or hobbyists but who are really trafficking firearms to felons or other prohibited persons.”<sup>25</sup></p> <p><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-25424" src="http://i0.wp.com/smartgunlaws.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/state-header.jpg?resize=500%2C41" alt="state-header" data-recalc-dims="1"></p> <p><strong>Seventeen states and D.C. have extended the background check requirement beyond federal law to at least some private sales.&nbsp;</strong>Six states (California, Colorado, Connecticut, Delaware, New York,&nbsp;Rhode Island) and&nbsp;D.C. require universal background checks at the point of sale for all transfers of all classes of firearms, including purchases from unlicensed sellers; Maryland and Pennsylvania laws do the same, but are limited to handguns. Two states (Illinois and Oregon) require a background check whenever a firearm in sold at a gun show.&nbsp; Finally, four states (Hawaii, Illinois, Massachusetts and New Jersey) require any firearm purchaser, including a purchaser from an unlicensed seller, to obtain a permit issued after a background check, and four more states (Iowa, Michigan, Nebraska and North Carolina) do the same only for handguns.<sup>26</sup></p> <p>Nevada and Oregon have laws allowing voluntary background checks by unlicensed sellers.</p> <p>Most of these jurisdictions also require unlicensed sellers to keep records of firearm sales or report such sales to law enforcement, as detailed in our summary on&nbsp;Maintaining Records&nbsp;&amp; Reporting Gun Sales.</p> <p><strong><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Description of State Laws Closing the Private Sale Loophole</span></strong></p> <p>1.&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <i>Background Checks at the Point of Transfer:</i>&nbsp; The most comprehensive approach to ensuring that guns are not sold to prohibited persons is through a requirement for&nbsp;a background check at the point of transfer of any firearm.&nbsp; Processing transfers by private sellers through licensed dealers or a law enforcement agency helps to ensure that a background check will be conducted prior to any transfer.</p> <p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">States that Require a Background Check at the Point of Transfer</span><br> California<br> Colorado<br> Connecticut<br> Delaware<br> District of Columbia<br> Maryland (handguns only)<br> New York<br> Pennsylvania (handguns only)<br> Rhode Island</p> <p>In California,<sup>27</sup>&nbsp;Colorado,<sup>28</sup>&nbsp;Delaware,<sup>29</sup>&nbsp;and New York<sup>30</sup>&nbsp;all firearm transfers must be processed through licensed dealers, who must conduct background checks on prospective firearm purchasers.&nbsp; Rhode Island requires all sellers to obtain a completed application form from the prospective purchaser, and to submit the form to law enforcement for purposes of conducting a background check.<sup>31</sup>&nbsp;Concealed handgun permit holders in Delaware and Rhode Island are exempt.&nbsp; Connecticut requires any person transferring a firearm to either submit a form to law enforcement or conduct the transfer through a licensed dealer, so that a background check is conducted for every sale or transfer.<sup>32</sup>&nbsp;In the District of Columbia, firearms may be transferred only by or to a licensed dealer.<sup>33</sup></p> <p>Maryland<sup>34</sup>&nbsp;and Pennsylvania<sup>35</sup>&nbsp;require a background check on every prospective transferee of a handgun, which may be conducted by a licensed dealer or a designated law enforcement agency.</p> <p>2.&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <i>Gun Show Background Checks:</i>&nbsp; Illinois<sup>36</sup>&nbsp;and Oregon<sup>37</sup>&nbsp;require a background check before the sale or transfer of a firearm at a gun show.&nbsp; For more information about the regulation of gun shows, see our summary on&nbsp;Gun Shows.</p> <p>3.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <i>State Permit Requirements for Private Purchasers:</i>&nbsp; Eight states regulate private sales primarily by prohibiting private sellers from transferring certain firearms to purchasers who do not have the requisite state license or permit, and requiring a background check before issuing the license or permit.</p> <p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">States that Require Permits for Private Purchasers After a Background Check</span><sup>38</sup><br> Hawaii<br> Illinois<br> Iowa (handguns only)<br> Massachusetts<br> Michigan (handguns only)<br> Nebraska (handguns only)<br> New Jersey<br> North Carolina (handguns only)</p> <p>More specifically, Hawaii,<sup>39</sup>&nbsp;Illinois,<sup>40</sup> Massachusetts<sup>41</sup>&nbsp;and New Jersey<sup>42</sup>&nbsp;require a person to obtain a license or permit before purchasing any firearm from any seller, and such license or permit cannot be obtained without a background check. Iowa,<sup>43</sup>&nbsp;Michigan,<sup>44</sup>&nbsp;Nebraska,<sup>45</sup>&nbsp;and North Carolina<sup>46</sup>&nbsp;require a person to obtain a license or permit before purchasing a handgun (but not a rifle or a shotgun) and require a background check before issuing the license or permit.&nbsp; These permits and licenses vary greatly in duration; as a result, there is a risk in some of these states that a person will become prohibited from purchasing a firearm after obtaining the license or permit but before purchasing a firearm.&nbsp; Illinois, on the other hand,&nbsp;now requires a seller to contact law enforcement and verify the validity of the purchaser’s permit (called a FOID Card) at the time of the sale, effective January 1, 2014.&nbsp;State licensing requirements are discussed in detail in our summary on&nbsp;Licensing Gun Owners&nbsp;&amp; Purchasers.<sup>47</sup></p> <p>4.&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <i>Voluntary Background Checks by Private Sellers:</i>&nbsp; In Nevada<sup>48</sup>&nbsp;and Oregon,<sup>49</sup>&nbsp;private sellers are not required to conduct background checks on purchasers (except, in Oregon, at gun shows), but they may request a background check of the purchaser.&nbsp; In Oregon and Nevada, the seller makes the request to the relevant state agency, which must process the request.&nbsp; In Oregon, subject to certain exceptions, a transferor who receives notification that the transferee is eligible to complete the transfer is immune from civil liability for any use of the firearm after the time of transfer.</p> <p>&nbsp;</p> <p><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-25422" src="http://i2.wp.com/smartgunlaws.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/comprehensive-law-header.jpg?resize=500%2C41" alt="comprehensive-law-header" data-recalc-dims="1"></p> <p>The features listed below are intended to provide a framework from which policy options may be considered.&nbsp; A jurisdiction considering new legislation should consult with counsel.</p> <ul> <li>For all firearm transfers, private sellers are subject to similar requirements as licensed dealers, including background checks and record keeping requirements:</li> <li>The most comprehensive option requires all firearm transfers to be conducted through licensed dealers, so that background checks will be completed on all purchasers (including purchases from unlicensed sellers), and sales records will be maintained <i>(California, Colorado, Delaware, District of Columbia, New York)</i></li> <li>If the jurisdiction does not require that all firearm transfers be conducted through licensed dealers, private sellers are required to: <ul style="text-align: left;"> <li>conduct background checks through a central law enforcement agency that has access to federal and state databases of prohibited purchasers <i>(Rhode Island requires private sellers to conduct background checks directly through law enforcement; Connecticut require private sellers to conduct background checks through licensed dealers or law enforcement);</i></li> <li>maintain records of all firearm transfers for a lengthy period<i> (Illinois requires all sellers to retain sales records for 10 years)</i>; and</li> <li>report all transfers to state and local law enforcement <i>(Connecticut, Hawaii, Massachusetts.</i></li> </ul> </li> </ul> </div> <p>Special Thanks to <a href="http://smartgunlaws.org" rel="nofollow">smartgunlaws.org</a></p> <div class="sharedaddy sd-sharing-enabled"><div class="robots-nocontent sd-block sd-social class="shadowblock_out post-1669 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-firearms-blog" id="post-1669"> <div class="shadowblock"> <div class="dashicons-before comment-bubble"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/what-is-swatting/#respond" class="bubble cp-fixed-color">0</a></div> <h3 class="loop"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/what-is-swatting/" title="What is SWATTING? What every Concealed Weapons License holder needs to know!">What is SWATTING? What every Concealed Weapons License holder needs to know!</a></h3> <p class="meta dotted"><span class="dashicons-before user"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/author/matt-adika/" title="Posts by Matt Adika" rel="author">Matt Adika</a></span> <span class="dashicons-before folderb"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/category/firearms-blog/" rel="category tag">Firearms Blog</a></span> <span class="dashicons-before clock"><span>November 7, 2014</span></span></p> <div class="entry-content"> <img width="150" height="95" src="http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/image.jpg?fit=150%2C95" class="attachment-blog-thumbnail size-blog-thumbnail wp-post-image" alt="Swatting" srcset="http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/image.jpg?w=640 640w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/image.jpg?resize=200%2C126 200w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/image.jpg?resize=500%2C317 500w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/image.jpg?resize=100%2C63 100w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/image.jpg?resize=150%2C95 150w" sizes="(max-width: 150px) 100vw, 150px"> <p>The pro-gun world is starting to hear more and more about members of the anti-gun crowd “SWATTING” gun owners, specifically open carriers.</p> <p>SWATTING, in case you haven’t heard, is the name people have given to the practice of calling the police and telling them someone has a gun and is actively shooting or planning to shoot innocent people. The goal is to cause a heavy-handed police response, with hopes of having the SWAT team arrive and storm the unsuspecting innocent with a violent and possibly deadly takedown. The video game crowd started SWATTING when the person about to lose the online video game would call 911 and send police to the home of his opponent.</p> <p>Of course it is illegal. It is making a false police report. But people still do it and now that anti-gun crowd has decided they should do it every time they see someone with a gun. It is especially easy when the target of the SWATTING is practicing open carry.</p> <p>The legal response to SWATTING should be swift and powerful for those people sending much-needed police assets against law-abiding citizens, but we can’t count on that. As long as these idiots can make anonymous reports, the police will still have to respond and gun owners will still be in danger during the police response.</p> <p>So here is my suggestion on how to deal with the situation should you be SWATTED by some idiotic anti-gunner.</p> <p>The first thing you need to remember is to keep your wits about you. If you and the family are just minding your own business at the mall and you are suddenly surrounded by police pointing guns at you and barking orders, I say follow those orders. Comply immediately. This is no time to become that guy who stands and argues, “I know my rights.” This is also no time to be the guy who starts hollering, “What is going on?” If you are on the business end of a heavy-handed police response, realize that you likely have been SWATTED and know that the person who called police told them you were an immediate threat and they should respond with force. Police arriving to such a call only know what the person on the other end of the line told the 911 operator. The caller could have said something like, “There was this guy threatening to shoot his wife if she didn’t shut up. He’s trying to act calm but he said he was going to kill her. You have to do something right away.”</p> <p>That puts the police in a tough spot and you in a tougher spot. So, comply with their orders, be polite, and follow instructions. You might be handcuffed. Officers might separate you and your wife for interviews. The cops will very likely take your gun while they are trying to sort things out. If you remain calm you will have a better chance of convincing the police on the scene that you are not a threat.</p> <p>Once the incident is winding down, it is time for you to start asking questions. Officers might not be able to tell you who called, but you can certainly let them know that you believe someone filed a false report and you want to make a complaint about that. Just remember to keep your cool. It may not be easy, because you have been wronged, but a calm demeanor will allow the situation to come back from the brink much more quickly.</p> <p>There is nothing good about this and we as gun owners have every right to be angry if it happens to us, but we need to be angry at the callers, not the police. Taking an aggressive posture with the police will only elevate the danger. This is not a simple traffic stop. This is a situation where a caller has tricked police into thinking they are entering a very volatile and dangerous situation. It’s not right, but you need to help defuse this thing.</p> <p>SWATTING is messed up on so many levels I can’t even begin to imagine what kind of idiot would do such a thing, but these are the kinds of idiots we deal with every day in the fight to protect our Second Amendment rights.</p> <p>Just one more thing law-abiding gun owners have to deal with.</p> <p>&nbsp;</p> <p>Special Thanks to <a title="US Concealed Carry" href="https://www.usconcealedcarry.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow">US Concealed Carry</a> for this great article.</p> <div class="sharedaddy sd-sharing-enabled"><div title="Click to share on Facebook"><span><span class="share-count">66</span></span><span class="sharing-screen-reader-text">Click to share on Facebook (Opens in new window)<span class="shadowblock_out post-1555 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-firearms-blog category-uncategorized tag-nra tag-firearm-training tag-florida-cwp tag-florida-firearms-training tag-gun-class tag-south-florida-firearms-training" id="post-1555"> <div class="shadowblock"> <div class="dashicons-before comment-bubble"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/south-florida-firearm-training/#respond" class="bubble cp-fixed-color">0</a></div> <h3 class="loop"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/south-florida-firearm-training/" title="NRA Blended Learning – South Florida Firearm Training">NRA Blended Learning – South Florida Firearm Training</a></h3> <p class="meta dotted"><span class="dashicons-before user"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/author/matt-adika/" title="Posts by Matt Adika" rel="author">Matt Adika</a></span> <span class="dashicons-before folderb"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/category/firearms-blog/" rel="category tag">Firearms Blog</a>, <a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/category/uncategorized/" rel="category tag">Uncategorized</a></span> <span class="dashicons-before clock"><span>October 17, 2014</span></span></p> <div class="entry-content"> <img width="150" height="88" src="http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image.jpg?fit=150%2C88" class="attachment-blog-thumbnail size-blog-thumbnail wp-post-image" alt="image" srcset="http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image.jpg?w=600 600w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image.jpg?resize=200%2C118 200w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image.jpg?resize=500%2C295 500w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image.jpg?resize=100%2C59 100w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image.jpg?resize=150%2C88 150w" sizes="(max-width: 150px) 100vw, 150px"> <p>&nbsp;</p> <h1>Looking South Florida Firearm Training?</h1> <h1>What is the benefit of having an NRA certified instructor teach my pistol training class?</h1> <p>Improvements to the NRA firearms training cirurricula have been steady throughout the years, starting with the development of student handbooks. NRA’s handbooks first contained hand-drawn images and have since evolved into black-and-white photographs and, more recently, high-resolution color photos. NRA’s course lesson plans have developed similarly, establishing learning objectives and helping instructors with time management. Overhead slides and PowerPoint presentations have allowed students to read information projected on a screen as the instructor taught the material. NRA created a warehouse and distribution system for easy ordering of the materials needed for each course, and <a href="http://NRAInstructors.org">NRAInstructors.org</a> has become an exclusive tool for NRA Instructors to market their courses to students and renewing their ratings from the NRA.</p> <p>The next innovation in firearms training is now upon us — blended learning. The blended learning teaching method combines an e-Learning student interface with instructor training and evaluation. The e-Learning portion will cover the curriculum that is currently being taught from the student handbook, and NRA Instructors will cover the hands-on firearm portions of the course, shooting exercises, the shooting qualification and make the final evaluation of the student.</p> <p>The blended learning method insures that each student receives course information in a consistent manner every time the course is given. In addition, students can now complete the classroom portion at their own pace, on their own schedule. This allows the instructor to focus on student education, safety and skills with a firearm. NRA Instructors will still determine which students have earned their certificates and which students need more training. NRA’s goal is to always be the standard when it comes to firearms safety, training and marksmanship. Blended learning is just another step in delivering on that standard.</p> <p><a href="http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image1.jpg" data-rel="colorbox"><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-1557" src="http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image1.jpg?resize=500%2C80" alt="image" srcset="http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image1.jpg?w=600 600w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image1.jpg?resize=200%2C32 200w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image1.jpg?resize=500%2C80 500w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image1.jpg?resize=100%2C16 100w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image1.jpg?resize=150%2C24 150w" sizes="(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px" data-recalc-dims="1"></a></p> <p><a href="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg" data-rel="colorbox"><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-1558" src="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?resize=108%2C24" alt="image" srcset="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?w=108 108w, http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?resize=100%2C22 100w" sizes="(max-width: 108px) 100vw, 108px" data-recalc-dims="1"></a></p> <p>I won’t be able to schedule my training because students have to complete a separate classroom segment.</p> <p><a href="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image3.jpg" data-rel="colorbox"><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-1559" src="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image3.jpg?resize=96%2C31" alt="NRA-Training-Fact" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><br> Instructors will still schedule the firearm segment classes but students will now have flexibility to complete the e-Learning classroom segment based on their schedule. Instructors will be able to schedule the firearm segment of each course in two ways. The first is on-demand, as students complete the e-Learning classroom segment. The second is to establish a date for the firearm segment and inform students that they will not be able to complete this without having successfully completed the e-Learning classroom segment in advance.</p> <p><a href="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg" data-rel="colorbox"><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-1558" src="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?resize=108%2C24" alt="image" srcset="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?w=108 108w, http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?resize=100%2C22 100w" sizes="(max-width: 108px) 100vw, 108px" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><br> Students who do not have computers or internet access will not be able to get training.<br> <a href="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image3.jpg" data-rel="colorbox"><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-1559" src="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image3.jpg?resize=96%2C31" alt="NRA-Training-Fact" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><br> Access to computers is widely available at public libraries in both rural and urban centers all over the country. The e-Learning classroom segment of the course will also be available using a mobile device such as a smartphone or a tablet. If the student is still unable to locate a computer, smartphone, or tablet, the instructor could secure access to one of these devices for them.</p> <p><a href="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg" data-rel="colorbox"><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-1558" src="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?resize=108%2C24" alt="image" srcset="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?w=108 108w, http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?resize=100%2C22 100w" sizes="(max-width: 108px) 100vw, 108px" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><br> The e-Learning classroom segment cannot be done in a group setting.<br> <a href="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image3.jpg" data-rel="colorbox"><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-1559" src="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image3.jpg?resize=96%2C31" alt="NRA-Training-Fact" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><br> NRA Instructors who want to do so can provide the necessary equipment for each student to complete the e-Learning classroom segment as a group.</p> <p><a href="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg" data-rel="colorbox"><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-1558" src="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?resize=108%2C24" alt="image" srcset="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?w=108 108w, http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?resize=100%2C22 100w" sizes="(max-width: 108px) 100vw, 108px" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><br> The e-Learning classroom segment is just a video the students watch.</p> <p><a href="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image3.jpg" data-rel="colorbox"><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-1559" src="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image3.jpg?resize=96%2C31" alt="NRA-Training-Fact" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><br> This e-Learning classroom segment is a learning management system that integrates the course content with interactive applications, lecture, animation, and review questions, which culminate in a final examination. The learning management system tracks students’ progress throughout the course, records, and missed exam answers. It provides materials for missed questions, and provides the instructor with information about the student before the firearm segment of the course.</p> <p><a href="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg" data-rel="colorbox"><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-1558" src="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?resize=108%2C24" alt="image" srcset="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?w=108 108w, http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?resize=100%2C22 100w" sizes="(max-width: 108px) 100vw, 108px" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><br> The blended learning course will be like the current Range Safety Officer course.</p> <p><a href="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image3.jpg" data-rel="colorbox"><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-1559" src="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image3.jpg?resize=96%2C31" alt="NRA-Training-Fact" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><br> The basic blended learning courses will be completely different, featuring both e-Learning classroom segment and an Instructor-led training segment.</p> <p><a href="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg" data-rel="colorbox"><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-1558" src="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?resize=108%2C24" alt="image" srcset="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?w=108 108w, http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?resize=100%2C22 100w" sizes="(max-width: 108px) 100vw, 108px" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><br> Students who live in states that don’t recognize e-Learning classes for concealed carry permits won’t be able to get one.</p> <p><a href="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image3.jpg" data-rel="colorbox"><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-1559" src="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image3.jpg?resize=96%2C31" alt="NRA-Training-Fact" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><br> This is NOT an e-Learning course, it is a blended learning course. Most states use the technique for delivering Hunter Education and Drivers Education. A live instructor is not required to show students the basic parts of a firearm, but with the blended learning system, a live instructor will ALWAYS have the final say as to when a student passes the basic course.<br> I will get fewer students because they have to go through an e-Learning class first.</p> <p><a href="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg" data-rel="colorbox"><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-1558" src="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?resize=108%2C24" alt="image" srcset="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?w=108 108w, http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?resize=100%2C22 100w" sizes="(max-width: 108px) 100vw, 108px" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><br> The ability for students to take the e-Learning classroom segment at any time, day or night, weekday or weekend, will increase the pool of students for you to evaluate and instruct. You will no longer need to rent a classroom where you will spend all of your day.</p> <p><a href="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image3.jpg" data-rel="colorbox"><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-1559" src="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image3.jpg?resize=96%2C31" alt="NRA-Training-Fact" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><br> NRA Instructors will not have the ability to price their own classes or determine if a student passes the course.<br> Instructors will still decide on the fee schedule, pre-range process and ultimately issue the NRA certificate. Students will not receive a certificate of completion for the NRA course until the instructor validates the student’s knowledge, skills, and attitude.</p> <p><a href="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg" data-rel="colorbox"><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-1558" src="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?resize=108%2C24" alt="image" srcset="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?w=108 108w, http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image2.jpg?resize=100%2C22 100w" sizes="(max-width: 108px) 100vw, 108px" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><br> Students will not be prepared for the Instructor-led training portion of the class.</p> <p><a href="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image3.jpg" data-rel="colorbox"><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-1559" src="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/image3.jpg?resize=96%2C31" alt="NRA-Training-Fact" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><br> Even though the student has taken the e-Learning classroom segment already, NRA Instructors will have a process in place to ensure the student meets the standards for the live fire portion. This may include a safety test or shortened classroom review. As always, NRA is relying on NRA Instructors to ensure each student meets the requirements to earn certification.</p> <p>Sign up for your NRA Basic Pistol Shooting course today @ Florida Gun Classifieds – 954.805.3440</p> <div class="sharedaddy sd-sharing-enabled"><div class="robots-nocontent sd-block sd-social sd-social-icon sd-sharing"><h3 class="sd-title">Share this for another entry class="dashicons-before comment-bubble"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/concealed-carry-firearm/#respond" class="bubble cp-fixed-color">0</a></div> <h3 class="loop"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/concealed-carry-firearm/" title="Story: My Concealed Carry Firearm Saved My Life">Story: My Concealed Carry Firearm Saved My Life</a></h3> <p class="meta dotted"><span class="dashicons-before user"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/author/matt-adika/" title="Posts by Matt Adika" rel="author">Matt Adika</a></span> <span class="dashicons-before folderb"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/category/firearms-blog/" rel="category tag">Firearms Blog</a>, <a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/category/uncategorized/" rel="category tag">Uncategorized</a></span> <span class="dashicons-before clock"><span>August 25, 2014</span></span></p> <div class="entry-content"> <img width="150" height="113" src="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Concealed-carry1.jpg?fit=150%2C113" class="attachment-blog-thumbnail size-blog-thumbnail wp-post-image" alt="florida concealed carry" srcset="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Concealed-carry1.jpg?w=600 600w, http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Concealed-carry1.jpg?resize=200%2C150 200w, http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Concealed-carry1.jpg?resize=500%2C376 500w, http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Concealed-carry1.jpg?resize=100%2C75 100w, http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Concealed-carry1.jpg?resize=150%2C113 150w" sizes="(max-width: 150px) 100vw, 150px"> <h1 style="text-align: center;"><em>Why Every&nbsp;American Should Carried a Concealed Firearm</em></h1> <h2>“Why do you have to carry a gun?”</h2> <h2>“What are you so afraid of?”</h2> <h2>“You must be really paranoid?”</h2> <h2>“If you pull your firearm, you must use it! are you ready to kill another human?”</h2> <p>These were some of the things I hear constantly from my Liberal friends. They live in their own bubble where the sexual assaults, rapes, and murders are just something you see on the nightly news, but could never happen to them and so they cannot understand why I have a<strong> Concealed Carry Firearm.&nbsp;</strong>I want to know that if god forbid I ever was confronted with one of these situations, I know I have a damn good chance of making it home that night. I choose to<strong> Carry a Concealed Firearm</strong> because I do not want to be one of those people on the 6:00 news that did make it home. They just don’t understand that criminals do not care who you are or what you have, some people in this world are just ruthless and will do anything to satisfy their evil desires.</p> <p style="text-align: justify;">My story is one of a woman traveling alone, in the middle of the day, on a rural highway and came up behind an older model, slow moving pickup truck with a middle aged man driving it. I noticed after a mile or two that he was making sexual gestures in his side mirror at me. So, the next opportunity I had to pass him, I did. Should be the end of that story, right? Well unfortunately it got much worse. Now he was tailgating me down the hill coming into town and now had my whole rear-view mirror to work with. He started taking off his shirt and looked to be touching himself. I was mortified to say the least. I blew through a yellow light and turned onto a busy highway and he stopped for the red light. I pulled into a gas station not far down the road because I needed to use the restroom and wanted to get something to drink. Not the best idea, looking back. I waited with my doors locked until I saw that he had moved on and passed me up. I had parked nose in facing the convenience store and he pulled in behind me and blocked my car in. This is when I grabbed my&nbsp;<strong>Concealed Carry Firearm</strong> a walther pk380 and had it ready to go. He came up to my door and reached for the handle only to see me holding my&nbsp;<strong>Concealed Carry Firearm</strong> in my hand and turning to aim at him. He just had to see the gun in my hands to send him scrambling back to his vehicle to hurry and drive away. I called in the plates to the police and it was all over with but I was on high alert for several days following. I have told my story countless times and about 70% of the time, someone will ignorantly say to me, <strong>“if you have to pull your firearm, you must use it!”</strong> I’m sorry but these people are very <strong>WRONG!</strong> In my case, I had several things working against my being able to shoot.</p> <p></p><center><p></p> <div id="fb-root" class=" fb_reset"><div style="position: absolute; top: -10000px; height: 0px; width: 0px;"><div><iframe name="fb_xdm_frame_http" frameborder="0" allowtransparency="true" allowfullscreen="true" scrolling="no" id="fb_xdm_frame_http" aria-hidden="true" title="Facebook Cross Domain Communication Frame" tabindex="-1" src="http://staticxx.facebook.com/connect/xd_arbiter.php?version=42#channel=f2b2b8122c&amp;origin=http%3A%2F%2Ffloridagunclassifieds.com" style="border: none;"></iframe><iframe name="fb_xdm_frame_https" frameborder="0" allowtransparency="true" allowfullscreen="true" scrolling="no" id="fb_xdm_frame_https" aria-hidden="true" title="Facebook Cross Domain Communication Frame" tabindex="-1" src="https://staticxx.facebook.com/connect/xd_arbiter.php?version=42#channel=f2b2b8122c&amp;origin=http%3A%2F%2Ffloridagunclassifieds.com" style="border: none;"></iframe></div></div><div style="position: absolute; top: -10000px; height: 0px; width: 0px;"><div></div></div></div> <p><script>// < ![CDATA[ <script>// < ![CDATA[ (function(d, s, id) { var js, fjs = d.getElementsByTagName(s)[0]; if (d.getElementById(id)) return; visibility: hidden;"></iframe></span></div> <p> </p></center><p></p> <ol> <li>He was at an angle next to my vehicle that I was not able to get a clear shot.</li> <li>Second, there were a lot of cars and people around and if I missed I could have hurt someone else who was not involved.</li> <li>Also, he was not carrying any kind of weapon to assault me with</li> </ol> <p>You always have to consider the aftermath of shooting someone in self defense. If all things were working together, I was prepared to shoot but my situational awareness kicked in and it was not a good option. There are other instances of not shooting but being able to safely mediate a situation just by having your firearm in hand. I recently watched this video which started my train of thought on writing this piece. Not every situation where you are forced to pull a firearm needs to end in tragedy. <a href="https://www.facebook.com/photo.php?v=637725659668551">Post</a> by <a href="https://urbanmoxy.wordpress.com/">Urban Moxy – Concealed Carry Handbags</a> The other example&nbsp;I can recall is the Clackamas mall shooting in Oregon a couple years ago. This was where I grew up&nbsp;so it hit very close to home and I visited the mall and paid my respects to the people who lost their lives on that tragic day. It could have been much worse than it turned out though. I think it was only reported locally that the shooter ended up killing himself because he saw a man had a pistol locked on him&nbsp;but was unable to shoot him because of all the people around and was not comfortable taking the shot at the risk of hurting another innocent person. The media didn’t spend very long on this story because it was very close to the Sandy Hook shooting but I think it was also because it had an outcome that didn’t agree with the anti-gun narrative. This man&nbsp;is the hero in my book! <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=58p1X-yOWy8">Concealed Carry</a></p> <div class="sharedaddy sd-sharing-enabled"><div class="robots-nocontent sd-block category-firearms-blog category-uncategorized" id="post-1116"> <div class="shadowblock"> <div class="dashicons-before comment-bubble"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/new-florida-concealed-weapons-law/#respond" class="bubble cp-fixed-color">0</a></div> <h3 class="loop"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/new-florida-concealed-weapons-law/" title="New Florida Concealed Weapons law: New Legislation that every concealed weapons licensee must know!">New Florida Concealed Weapons law: New Legislation that every concealed weapons licensee must know!</a></h3> <p class="meta dotted"><span class="dashicons-before user"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/author/matt-adika/" title="Posts by Matt Adika" rel="author">Matt Adika</a></span> <span class="dashicons-before folderb"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/category/firearms-blog/" rel="category tag">Firearms Blog</a>, <a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/category/uncategorized/" rel="category tag">Uncategorized</a></span> <span class="dashicons-before clock"><span>July 1, 2014</span></span></p> <div class="entry-content"> <img width="150" height="98" src="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/07/gunlaw.jpg?fit=150%2C98" class="attachment-blog-thumbnail size-blog-thumbnail wp-post-image" alt="Florida Concealed Carry Law" srcset="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/07/gunlaw.jpg?w=278 278w, http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/07/gunlaw.jpg?resize=200%2C130 200w, http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/07/gunlaw.jpg?resize=100%2C65 100w, http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/07/gunlaw.jpg?resize=150%2C98 150w" sizes="(max-width: 150px) 100vw, 150px"> <h1>NEW Florida Concealed Weapons Law: New Legislation that every concealed weapons licensee must know!</h1> <h2>Governor Rick Scott Signs 36 Bills into Law</h2> <h3>Governor Rick Scott signed the following bills into law today:</h3> <p>HB 21 The bill requires the Department of Education to create a uniform, statewide photo identification badge signifying that a noninstructional contractor meets certain background screening and other requirements.</p> <p>CS/SB 56 The bill updates the protocols of the Department of Health and medical examiners when reporting and classifying the cause of death of an infant under one year of age who suddenly dies when in apparent good health.</p> <p>CS/HB 93 The bill allows individuals obtaining or renewing their motor vehicle registration or driver license to make a voluntary contribution of $1.00 to assist the homeless.</p> <p>CS/CS/HB 113 The bill creates a new offense making it a third-degree felony for an adult to knowingly distribute material harmful to a minor or post materials harmful to a minor on public and private school property.</p> <p>CS/HB 135 The bill designates the following Brevard County properties as spaceport territory: the Space Coast Regional Airport, the Space Coast Industrial Park, and the Spaceport Commerce Park.</p> <p>CS/CS/HB 277 The bill prevents an increase in the assessed value of residential properties as a result of installing a renewable energy source device.</p> <p>CS/SB 284 The bill establishes a process for private schools to register to be notified at the same time public school districts are notified about an emergency occurrence in the local area that could threaten student safety. The bill also allows school districts, or private schools, to adopt a protocol developed by a licensed physician for the administration of epinephrine auto-injection by trained school personnel.</p> <p>CS/CS/CS/HB 319 The bill makes changes to local transportation concurrency options which are designed to ensure transportation facilities and services are available and kept concurrent with local development.</p> <p>SB 342 The bill allows the rental of homestead properties to be rented for up to 30 days a calendar year while maintaining the homestead classification.</p> <p>CS/CS/CS/HB 375 The bill provides that the owner of a residence may be approved and permitted by the Department of Health as a maintenance entity for their own engineer-designed Onsite Sewage Treatment &amp; Disposal System or Aerobic Treatment Unit.</p> <p>HB 407 This bill protects Florida’s children by enhancing criminal penalties against convicted gang members who trespass in school safety zones and provides enhanced criminal penalties for any person who solicits or recruits children under age 13 into a gang.</p> <p>CS/CS/HB 411 The bill codifies the two existing children’s initiatives in Orlando and Jacksonville in statute.</p> <p>CS/HB 423 The bill exempts dyed diesel fuel used for commercial fishing and aquaculture purposes from the sales and use tax</p> <p>CS/CS/HB 437 The bill clarifies Florida Housing Finance Corporation’s corporate roles and responsibilities.</p> <p>SB 452 The bill permanently reauthorizes the public records exemption for a donor’s personal identifying information, held in the Joshua Abbott Organ and Tissue Registry.</p> <p>CS/HB 461 The bill requires the Department of Education, in coordination with the Florida School for the Deaf and Blind and with input from stakeholders including representatives of the auditory oral community, to develop a model communications plan for use during the individual educational plan development.</p> <p>CS/CS/SB 468 The bill codifies a pilot project by the Office of Insurance Regulation that provides an alternative mechanism to the insurance policy form filing and approval process for property and casualty insurance lines, excluding workers’ compensation and personal lines.</p> <p>CS/CS/CS/HB 487 The bill creates the Freemasonry specialty license plate, establishes the annual use fee of $25, and provides that those funds will benefit the Masonic Home Endowment Fund, Inc.</p> <p>CS/CS/HB 609 The bill amends the definition of bullying to include cyberbullying, and establishes new prohibitions for technology-related activities that adversely affects the ability of a student to receive an education or that disrupts the orderly operation of school.</p> <p>SB 628 The bill provides a public record exemption for reproductions of photographic or digital images from the Department of Highway Safety and Motor Vehicles Driver and Vehicle Information Database for the certain people as part of their official work of the court.</p> <p>CS/CS/SB 682 The bill provides for the approval and standards of certain beneficial uses of fossil fuel combustion products, the waste byproducts of burning fossil fuels. It also provides that the prohibition against hazardous waste landfills in Florida would not be applicable to these waste byproducts, should the United States Environmental Protection Agency deem them hazardous waste.</p> <p>CS/CS/CS/HB 701 The bill prohibits the use or acceptance of electronic benefits transfer cards at establishments licensed to sell distilled spirits, adult entertainment establishments, pari-mutuel facilities, slot machine facilities, commercial bingo facilities, casinos, gaming and gambling facilities.</p> <p>CS/CS/HB 801 The bill substitutes “certified school counselor” for the term “guidance counselor” to reflect the current requirement that persons employed as public school counselors be certified.</p> <p>CS/HB 841 The bill provides clarification and consistency in use of a power of attorney, which is a legal document that a person can use to authorize another person to act on his or her behalf.</p> <p>CS/HB 969 The bill provides statutory guidance to streamline the regulatory process for recreational vehicle parks and recreational camps when applying for a permit with the Department of Health and redefines the term “occupancy.”</p> <p>CS/CS/CS/HB 999 The bill addresses issues ranging from special event permitting at boat shows to permitting authority for water wells to expedited permitting for natural gas pipelines.</p> <p>CS/HB 1071 The bill amends various sections of Florida law in order to provide a standard definition and a uniform interpretation and application of the term accrediting organization.</p> <p>HB 1157 The bill eliminates the sunset date of the health flex plan program. Health flex plans were established to provide affordable health care services to low-income uninsured Floridians.</p> <p>CS/HB 1193 The bill strikes three of the five conditions resulting in the loss of the agricultural classification of land and removes the authority of the Value Adjustment Board to review land classifications and property exemptions upon its own motion.</p> <p>CS/SB 1768 The bill permanently reauthorizes the public records exemption for individuals who apply for or receive paratransit services. Paratransit services are special transportation services to assist individuals who cannot otherwise access the public transportation system, such as persons with disabilities.</p> <p>SB 1806 The bill provides that the Florida Department of Environmental Protection’s rules on Total Maximum Daily Loads are exempt from legislative ratification requirements.</p> <p>CS/SB 1808 The bill establishes the manner by which the Florida Department of Environmental Protection (DEP) is to proceed with outstanding numeric nutrient criteria rulemaking and represents a key aspect to recovering state control over Florida’s waters from the United States Environmental Protection Agency.</p> <p>SB 1830 The bill streamlines the administration of the property tax, clarifies that counties are authorized to grant an additional homestead exemption of up to $50,000 to qualifying low income seniors, and broadens the ad valorem tax discount provided to disabled veterans to include veterans who were not Florida residents at the time of entering military service.</p> <p>SB 1850 The bill exempts from public record the proprietary business information that is owned or controlled by an insurer participating in the Citizens Property Insurance Corporation clearinghouse program created in SB 1770 (Note: this bill was filed yesterday 5/29).</p> <p>HB 4013 The bill eliminates the lifetime maximum amount of tax refunds a business could receive under the Qualified Target Industry ($7 million or $7.5 million if located in an enterprise zone) and Qualified Defense and Space Flight Business Programs ($7 million).</p> <p>HB 7143 The bill reauthorizes the public records and public meeting exemptions for donors to direct-support organizations for the Department of Veterans Affairs.</p> <div category-firearms-blog category-uncategorized tag-concealed-carry-draw tag-how-to tag-how-to-carry-concealed tag-how-to-defend-yourself tag-how-to-draw-a-weapon tag-how-to-draw-from-concealed-carry tag-how-to-guns tag-training" id="post-1086"> <div class="shadowblock"> <div class="dashicons-before comment-bubble"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/how-to-draw-a-gun-from-a-holster/#comments" class="bubble cp-fixed-color">1</a></div> <h3 class="loop"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/how-to-draw-a-gun-from-a-holster/" title="Video: How to Draw a Gun From a Holster? – One Hand Concealed Carry Draw – Concealed Holster Training Drills">Video: How to Draw a Gun From a Holster? – One Hand Concealed Carry Draw – Concealed Holster Training Drills</a></h3> <p class="meta dotted"><span class="dashicons-before user"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/author/matt-adika/" title="Posts by Matt Adika" rel="author">Matt Adika</a></span> <span class="dashicons-before folderb"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/category/firearms-blog/" rel="category tag">Firearms Blog</a>, <a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/category/uncategorized/" rel="category tag">Uncategorized</a></span> <span class="dashicons-before clock"><span>June 27, 2014</span></span></p> <div class="entry-content"> <img width="150" height="150" src="http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/concealed-carry-draw.jpg?fit=150%2C150" class="attachment-blog-thumbnail size-blog-thumbnail wp-post-image" alt="how to draw a gun from a holster" srcset="http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/concealed-carry-draw.jpg?w=300 300w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/concealed-carry-draw.jpg?resize=50%2C50 50w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/concealed-carry-draw.jpg?resize=150%2C150 150w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/concealed-carry-draw.jpg?resize=100%2C100 100w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/concealed-carry-draw.jpg?resize=75%2C75 75w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/concealed-carry-draw.jpg?resize=250%2C250 250w" sizes="(max-width: 150px) 100vw, 150px"> <h1>How to Draw a Gun From a Holster? –&nbsp;One Hand Concealed Carry Draw – Concealed Holster Training Drills</h1> <h2>Brent takes us through his process of how to draw a gun from a holster. His technique is always drawing his concealed weapon with one hand.</h2> <h3>As the video will show, with practice this can be just as fast as a traditional two handed draw. Brent emphisizes the importance of training and practicing at the range&nbsp;using real life&nbsp;senarios. If you are not comfortable using live ammunition to practice drawing your firearm from a concealed carry holster, ALWAYS practice with your firearm unloaded to get the motion down before attempting to use live ammunition&nbsp;at the range. This is extremely important. Safety should always be at the forefront of any gun owner’s mind especially when carrying a firearm. As my last blog on “Choosing the best gun for concealed carry” states, the holster is just as important as the gun. Make sure your holster is the correct fit for your gun. Kydex is usually the best way to secure your firearm because it has some retention. Retention puts pressure on a area of the gun, usually the trigger gaurd to securly “snap” the gun into the holster. There should be just enough retention to securely “snap” the gun in place and keep it there, but not enough where you have to struggle to draw your firearm.</h3> <p><strong>Always obey the firearms rules of safety&nbsp;when learning how to draw a gun from a holster which are</strong>:</p> <ol> <li>ALWAYS treat any firearm as if it were loaded.</li> <li>ALWAYS keep the gun pointed in a safe direction.</li> <li>ALWAYS keep your finger off the trigger until ready to shoot.</li> </ol> <p>Watch the video below by Brent to learn <strong>how to draw a gun from a holster</strong> correctly.</p> category-firearms-blog category-uncategorized" id="post-1068"> <div class="shadowblock"> <div class="dashicons-before comment-bubble"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/best-gun-concealed-carry/#comments" class="bubble cp-fixed-color">3</a></div> <h3 class="loop"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/best-gun-concealed-carry/" title="What is the best gun for concealed carry?">What is the best gun for concealed carry?</a></h3> <p class="meta dotted"><span class="dashicons-before user"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/author/matt-adika/" title="Posts by Matt Adika" rel="author">Matt Adika</a></span> <span class="dashicons-before folderb"><a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/category/firearms-blog/" rel="category tag">Firearms Blog</a>, <a href="http://floridagunclassifieds.com/category/uncategorized/" rel="category tag">Uncategorized</a></span> <span class="dashicons-before clock"><span>June 27, 2014</span></span></p> <div class="entry-content"> <img width="150" height="113" src="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Concealed-carry1.jpg?fit=150%2C113" class="attachment-blog-thumbnail size-blog-thumbnail wp-post-image" alt="florida concealed carry" srcset="http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Concealed-carry1.jpg?w=600 600w, http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Concealed-carry1.jpg?resize=200%2C150 200w, http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Concealed-carry1.jpg?resize=500%2C376 500w, http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Concealed-carry1.jpg?resize=100%2C75 100w, http://i1.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Concealed-carry1.jpg?resize=150%2C113 150w" sizes="(max-width: 150px) 100vw, 150px"> <h1 style="text-align: center;">Concealed Carry: What is the best gun for concealed carry?</h1> <p>&nbsp;</p> <h2>To determine what is the best gun for concealed carry you first have to look at the individual that will be carrying the firearm and ask yourself a couple of key questions:</h2> <ul> <li>How do you normally dress?</li> <li>Do you always wear a belt?</li> <li>Is your wardrobe tight fitting or loose?</li> <li>How much experience do you have with firearms?</li> </ul> <h3>These are all questions that should be considered and&nbsp;addressed before searching the gun listings on Florida Gun Classifieds, to help you zero in on a specific gun to carry on a daily basis. Searching the <strong>Gun listings on Florida Gun Classifieds</strong> for <strong>guns for sale</strong> to find t<strong>he best concealed carry firearm is a good way to find a gun that you will actually carry everyday, every night, everywhere you go. If you decide to do what I did when I first started carrying a firearm, to get the biggest, baddest gun with the most capacity and the largest caliber, I promise you that will&nbsp;probably&nbsp;last for about a&nbsp;month. You eventually will decide, “I’m just going&nbsp;down the street to the gas station, I’m not going to need it, ill just leave it in the safe.” and you’ll find any excuse not to bring the gun for the simple fact its too damn heavy and uncomfortable! Then you will be back searching the gun listings on Florida Gun Classifieds for guns for sale real quick.&nbsp;I learned my lesson on that one.</strong></h3> <p>&nbsp;</p> <h3><strong>The best gun for concealed carry is a firearm that will feel like you are not carrying a gun, almost like your phone does in your pocket. The gun must be easily accessible and you must know the firearm inside and out. While searching the gun listings on Florida Gun Classifieds for guns for sale make sure you keep this in mind. One way to ensure you will be carrying correctly is to spend the money on a good quality holster. A holster should fit your specific firearm like a glove, covering the trigger guard completely. Weather you chose inside or outside the waist, the gun should be able to be drawn without any delay or obstruction. This goes back to the question about what type of clothes do you normally wear. If you wardrobe consists of jeans, a belt and loose fitting shirts, then an outside the pants holster will be the holster of choice. The outside the pants holster will always be more comfortable then an inside the waist holster. It will allow you to carry the firearm securely and also access the firearm quickly, while allowing you&nbsp;flexibility&nbsp;to do things such as get in and out of your&nbsp;car with ease, sit down comfortably without being stuck in the stomach and encourage you to carry more often than not. There are different&nbsp;versions&nbsp;of outside the pants holsters, and my favorite is a leather/kydex hybrid that securely holds the firearm, while&nbsp;providing the comfort of leather against the body.</strong></h3> <h4>If your wardrobe consists of mostly shorts without a belt, basketball shorts, t-shirts etc, then an inside the pants holster is probably the best choice. There are different versions of these available as well from leather, kydex, and also synthetic materials. My preference is a small leather or kydex IWB (inside the waistband) holster that covers the trigger guard completely. This will provide just enough material to securely hold the firearm while keeping the gun at a fingertips reach securely in place wherever you clip it. It should not&nbsp;move or slide&nbsp;around on your waist. While viewing the gun listings on Florida Gun Classifieds for your perfect concealed carry gun for sale, think about how you will be carrying the firearm before making a decision.</h4> <h4>With any concealed firearm, training is an essential part of carrying. Without adequate practice drawing your firearm, the&nbsp;same gun you are concealing to protect yourself is essentially useless. The FBI statistics are that the&nbsp;average self defense shooting happens in under&nbsp;three seconds and consists of three shots. If you have to fumble to draw your firearm, you are too late. You should be able to draw&nbsp;your gun in under a second, and&nbsp;shoot&nbsp;at least two&nbsp;shots without aiming.&nbsp;This takes practice, especially to be accurate! &nbsp;If you think buying a gun and sticking it in your pants will protect you from the bad guys, think again.&nbsp;Without adequate training your firearm is useless, and can even be used against you. You will find all kinds of guns for sale by viewing the gun&nbsp;listings on Florida Gun Classifieds. After purchasing a gun it is essential that you either practice with that firearm until you can draw, shoot and re-holster without hesitation.</h4> <h4>I laugh at people that tell me they do not carry a round in the chamber, and then try to educate them on the reality that you will not have time to rack the slide in a real life self defense situation. If you do have time to rack the slide and draw down on someone, is it really an IMMEDIATE THREAT? Think about this: Imagine your life is in imminent danger and there is a camera&nbsp;surveilling&nbsp;the area. Your attacker approaches and you draw your firearm, hold it up, rack the slide, draw down on your attacker and shoot. Think about how that would look on the camera or how it would look to a jury. Although you might be legally justified, it looks horrible and a anti-gun prosecutor would try to take you down. Now the same situation with a round already chambered. You pull your firearm and shoot. Can you see how each scenario looks to an average person or juror with little or no firearm experience?</h4> <h4>The best way&nbsp;to select a concealed carry firearm from the&nbsp;<strong>gun listings on Florida Gun Classifieds is to&nbsp;find a gun for sale that fits</strong>&nbsp;your wardrobe, obtain a proper holster and get professional training to build your skills. This is the key to concealed carry to encourage you&nbsp;to carry 100% of the time comfortably and ready for the&nbsp;unthinkable.</h4> <div id="attachment_179" style="width: 211px" class="wp-caption alignleft"><a class="cboxElement" href="http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/matt.jpg" data-rel="colorbox"><img class="wp-image-179" src="http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/matt.jpg?resize=201%2C201" alt="Gun Listings, Florida Guns for sale" srcset="http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/matt.jpg?w=558 558w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/matt.jpg?resize=50%2C50 50w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/matt.jpg?resize=150%2C150 150w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/matt.jpg?resize=500%2C500 500w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/matt.jpg?resize=100%2C100 100w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/matt.jpg?resize=75%2C75 75w, http://i2.wp.com/floridagunclassifieds.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/matt.jpg?resize=250%2C250 250w" sizes="(max-width: 201px) 100vw, 201px" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><p class="wp-caption-text">Matt Adika – Florida Gun Classifieds</p></div> <p>&nbsp;</p> <p>&nbsp;</p> <p>&nbsp;</p> <p>&nbsp;</p>
